<p>"<b>Womanizer</b>" is a song recorded by American singer <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> for her sixth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Circus_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Circus (Britney Spears album)">Circus</a></i> (2008). It was released on October 3, 2008 by <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> of the album. Produced and co-written by Nikesha Briscoe and Rafael Akinyemi of <a href="/wiki/The_Outsyders" title="The Outsyders">The Outsyders</a>, the song was re-recorded after a snippet was leaked onto the internet. "Womanizer" is an up-tempo <a href="/wiki/Electropop" title="Electropop">electropop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> song. Described by Spears as a girl <a href="/wiki/Anthem" title="Anthem">anthem</a>, the song's lyrics recall a womanizing man, while the protagonist of the song makes clear she knows who he really is. Music critics mostly praised its hook, melody and empowering lyrics. Critics also observed it was a stand-out track from its album and also deemed it as a comeback single for Spears.</p>
<p>"Womanizer" was a commercial success, peaking atop of the charts in Belgium, Canada, Denmark, Finland, France, Norway, Sweden and the United States. It also reached the top ten in every country it charted in also receiving several certifications from several countries. In the United States, "Womanizer" was her first single to reach number-one since "<a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)" title="...Baby One More Time (song)">...Baby One More Time</a>" in 1999. The song broke the record for the highest jump to number one at a time which was later broken by <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/My_Life_Would_Suck_Without_You" title="My Life Would Suck Without You">My Life Would Suck Without You</a>" in 2009. It is also her best-selling digital song in the country, having sold over 5 million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_sales_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-us_sales-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kahn" title="Joseph Kahn">Joseph Kahn</a>, was created by Spears as a sequel to the music video of "<a href="/wiki/Toxic_(song)" title="Toxic (song)">Toxic</a>". It portrays Spears as a woman who disguises herself in different costumes and follows her boyfriend through his daily activities to expose him in the end. The video also contains interspersed scenes of Spears naked in a steam room, as a response to the attacks she had received over the years about her weight. The video was also nominated for two categories at the <a href="/wiki/2009_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2009 MTV Video Music Awards">2009 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, and went on to win <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Pop_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Pop Video">Best Pop Video</a>.</p>
<p>The song has been covered by a number of artists from different genres, including <a href="/wiki/Lily_Allen" title="Lily Allen">Lily Allen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Ferdinand_(band)" title="Franz Ferdinand (band)">Franz Ferdinand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Girls_Aloud" title="Girls Aloud">Girls Aloud</a>. Spears performed "Womanizer" on several television shows including <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_TV_series)" title="The X Factor (UK TV series)">The X Factor</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i>, as well as award shows such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bambi_Awards" title="Bambi Awards">2008 Bambi Awards</a>. She has also performed the song at <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a> (2009), the <a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_Tour" title="Femme Fatale Tour">Femme Fatale Tour</a> (2011) and <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a> (2013). "Womanizer" received a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/52nd_Grammy_Awards" title="52nd Grammy Awards">Grammy</a> nomination in 2010 in the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Dance_Recording" title="Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording">Best Dance Recording</a> category, but lost to <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Poker_Face_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Poker Face (Lady Gaga song)">Poker Face</a>".</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The song was written and co-produced by Nikesha Briscoe and Rafael Akinyemi of the production team, <a href="/wiki/The_Outsyders" title="The Outsyders">The Outsyders</a>. Spears recorded main vocals with Brendan Dakora at Glenwood Place Studios in <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank, California</a> and Bojan "Genius" Dugic at Legacy Studios in New York City. <a href="/wiki/Pro_Tools" title="Pro Tools">Pro Tools engineering</a> was done by John Hanes, assisted by Tim Roberts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-liner-2">[2]</a></sup> On September 19, 2008, a low quality 37 second snippet of the song was posted on the official website of <a href="/wiki/WRVW" title="WRVW">107.5 The River</a>, a radio station in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon,_Tennessee" title="Lebanon, Tennessee">Lebanon, Tennessee</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a>, a representative of the label played a rough <a href="/wiki/Audio_mixing_(recorded_music)" title="Audio mixing (recorded music)">mix</a> of the song for people at the station, who recorded it and leaked it on the Internet. The snippet was later removed from the website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snippet_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-snippet-3">[3]</a></sup> The song was scheduled to premiere on September 23, 2008, but the release was delayed when Spears went into the studio to re-record some vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daily_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-daily-4">[4]</a></sup> The new recordings were done with <a href="/wiki/Jim_Beanz" title="Jim Beanz">Jim Beanz</a> and Marcella "Ms. Lago" Araica.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvd_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-dvd-5">[5]</a></sup> The song was finally mixed by Serban Ghenea at MixStar Studios in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-liner-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stuff_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-stuff-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_lyrics">Music and lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Music and lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Womanizer_-_Britney_Spears.ogg" title="File:Womanizer - Britney Spears.ogg">Womanizer</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="24.978752834467" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="Womanizer_-_Britney_Spears.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px">
<source data-bandwidth="66517" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (67 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/51/Womanizer_-_Britney_Spears.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'></source></audio></div>
</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">The pre-chorus of "Womanizer", in which the title is repeated eight times.</div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>"Womanizer" is an uptempo <a href="/wiki/Electropop" title="Electropop">electropop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> song with dark synths that runs through a <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance oriented beat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daily_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-daily-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> It has been compared to previous Spears' songs such as "<a href="/wiki/Toxic_(song)" title="Toxic (song)">Toxic</a>" (2004) and "Ooh Ooh Baby" (2007).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popjustice_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-popjustice-8">[8]</a></sup> It is written in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Song_structure_(popular_music)#Verse" title="Song structure (popular music)">verse</a>–<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Song_structure_(popular_music)#Pre-chorus" title="Song structure (popular music)">pre-chorus</a>–<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Song_structure_(popular_music)#Chorus" title="Song structure (popular music)">chorus</a> form. The track opens with its characteristical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siren_(noisemaker)" title="Siren (noisemaker)">sirens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardiansingle_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardiansingle-9">[9]</a></sup> According to Ann Powers of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, Spears "quick-witted" vocals are similar to the style of <a href="/wiki/The_Andrews_Sisters" title="The Andrews Sisters">The Andrews Sisters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-10">[10]</a></sup> It was also noted by <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">Daily News</a></i> writer Jim Farber that Spears' delivery has a "tone of petulance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daily_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-daily-4">[4]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(music)" title="Bridge (music)">bridge</a>, Spears sings the chorus one more time and the song ends while the beat drops and Spears sings the "you’re a womanizer, baby" <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popjustice_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-popjustice-8">[8]</a></sup> The song is set in a 12/8 time signature and composed in the key of <a href="/wiki/C-sharp_minor" title="C-sharp minor">C<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;">♯</span> minor</a> with 139 <a href="/wiki/Tempo" title="Tempo">beats per minute</a>. The chord progression in the song is C#m-F#m-E-D#-D. Lyrically, the song refers to a <a href="/wiki/Promiscuity#Male_promiscuity" title="Promiscuity">womanizing</a> man.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-10">[10]</a></sup> It has been suggested that the lyrics address Spears' ex-husband <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Federline" title="Kevin Federline">Kevin Federline</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daily_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-daily-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_London.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_London.jpg/220px-Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_London.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_London.jpg/330px-Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_London.jpg/440px-Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_London.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_London.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears performing "Womanizer" at <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Upon release, the song received mostly positive reviews from contemporary music critics. Peter Robinson of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> gave the song the maximum <a href="/wiki/Star_(classification)" title="Star (classification)">five stars</a> referring to it as a "comeback single" and as having a "genius <a href="/wiki/Hook_(music)" title="Hook (music)">hook</a>". He added that the song "[has] been called lazy, largely by misinformed people who also think that <a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Get_You_Out_of_My_Head" title="Can't Get You Out of My Head">'la la la's</a> would have been better with proper words".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-observer_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-observer-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Popjustice" title="Popjustice">Popjustice</a> compared it to "<a href="/wiki/Some_Girls_(Rachel_Stevens_song)" title="Some Girls (Rachel Stevens song)">Some Girls</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Stevens" title="Rachel Stevens">Rachel Stevens</a> and added "[The] track lays a really strong foundation for the fully-realised comeback that didn't quite happen last time and it's hard not to think of it as a late contender for single of the year. [...] It's literally quite good".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popjustice_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-popjustice-8">[8]</a></sup> Myrddin Gwynedd of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Zealand_Herald" title="The New Zealand Herald">The New Zealand Herald</a></i> said "it's got <a href="/wiki/Hit_single" title="Hit single">hit</a> written all over it".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newzealand_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-newzealand-12">[12]</a></sup> On the week of November 24, 2008, the <i><a href="/wiki/Derby_Telegraph" title="Derby Telegraph">Derby Telegraph</a></i> chose it as single of the week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-derby_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-derby-13">[13]</a></sup> In the album review, Nekesa Mumbi Moody of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Providence_Journal" title="The Providence Journal">The Providence Journal</a></i> said that along with "Shattered Glass", they were "[two] fun disco tracks".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nekesa_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-nekesa-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> writer Steve Jones named it one of the standout tracks of the album and commented that "she seems most at ease when she's playing the teasing tart".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-15">[15]</a></sup> Talia Kraines of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> commented that Spears needed more songs like "Womanizer", saying "Britney 2.0 needs to be full of wild dancefloor driven moves".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-16">[16]</a></sup> Simon Price of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> commented the song borrows its <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic sound</a> from <a href="/wiki/Goldfrapp" title="Goldfrapp">Goldfrapp</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent-17">[17]</a></sup> Ann Powers of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> complimented Spears' delivery and the lyrics, saying the song is "about the kind of <a href="/wiki/Girl_power" title="Girl power">girl power</a> that's focused on besting one obnoxious man, is also <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vintage" title="wiktionary:vintage">vintage</a> and contemporary at the same time – more feminism as <a href="/wiki/Individualism" title="Individualism">individualism</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-10">[10]</a></sup> Mike Newmark of <a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a> called the song " a meaty, high-voltage shuffler helmed by the Outsyders, who do an admirable job of recreating the chemistry of Spears and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danja_(musician)" title="Danja (musician)">Danja</a> on last year’s single '<a href="/wiki/Gimme_More" title="Gimme More">Gimme More</a>'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popmatters_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-popmatters-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Jim Farber of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daily_News_(New_York)" title="Daily News (New York)">Daily News</a></i> said the pre-chorus was the most repetitive in a pop song since <a href="/wiki/The_Shaggs" title="The Shaggs">The Shaggs</a>'s "Gimmie Dat Ding".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-daily_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-daily-4">[4]</a></sup> Jim Abbott of the <i><a href="/wiki/Orlando_Sentinel" title="Orlando Sentinel">Orlando Sentinel</a></i> called it "basically an adult update of her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teen-pop" title="Teen-pop">teen-pop</a> tease act".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orlando_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-orlando-19">[19]</a></sup> Ian Watson of <a href="/wiki/Dotmusic" title="Dotmusic">Dotmusic</a> wrote that Spears sounded "trapped on this single. Not trapped, as in desperate and distraught, but trapped as in literally frozen – like she's been placed into a robot on a production line and she has to sing these words, dance these steps, work it like this, until the spotlight snaps off and the factory's powered down for the night".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dot_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-dot-20">[20]</a></sup> The song has been nominated for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/52nd_Grammy_Awards" title="52nd Grammy Awards">Grammy Award</a> in the category of <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Dance_Recording" title="Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording">Best Dance Recording</a> on December 2, 2009. Spears had previously won the category in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/47th_Grammy_Awards" title="47th Grammy Awards">the 2005 ceremony</a> for her single "Toxic".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> However, it lost to <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Poker_Face_(Lady_Gaga_song)" title="Poker Face (Lady Gaga song)">Poker Face</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_(Live_in_Ukraine).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="762" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_%28Live_in_Ukraine%29.jpg/170px-Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_%28Live_in_Ukraine%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_%28Live_in_Ukraine%29.jpg/255px-Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_%28Live_in_Ukraine%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_%28Live_in_Ukraine%29.jpg/340px-Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_%28Live_in_Ukraine%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_-_Womanizer_(Live_in_Ukraine).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears performing "Womanizer" at the <a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_Tour" title="Femme Fatale Tour">Femme Fatale Tour</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the United States, the song entered the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> at number ninety-six on the issue dated October 8, 2008. The following week, the song jumped to number one breaking the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">records</a> for largest jump to number one and largest jump to any position in the history of the chart, previously held by <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Live_Your_Life_(T.I._song)" title="Live Your Life (T.I. song)">Live Your Life</a>" (feat. <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Liar" title="Beautiful Liar">Beautiful Liar</a>", respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbjump_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbjump-23">[23]</a></sup> The record was later broken by <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/My_Life_Would_Suck_Without_You" title="My Life Would Suck Without You">My Life Would Suck Without You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kelly_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-kelly-24">[24]</a></sup> It also garnered first-week <a href="/wiki/Music_download" title="Music download">download</a> sales of 286,000, the biggest opening-week tally by a female artist since <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> began tracking digital downloads in 2003, surpassing the record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>'s "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Touch_My_Body_(Mariah_Carey_song)" title="Touch My Body (Mariah Carey song)">Touch My Body</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbjump_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbjump-23">[23]</a></sup> The record was broken on January 27, 2010 by <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Today_Was_a_Fairytale" title="Today Was a Fairytale">Today Was a Fairytale</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-taylor_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-taylor-25">[25]</a></sup> "Womanizer" was Spears' first number one single since her debut "<a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)" title="...Baby One More Time (song)">...Baby One More Time</a>" in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbjump_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbjump-23">[23]</a></sup> On the week of January 3, 2009, the song reached number one on the <i>Billboard</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pop_Songs" title="Pop Songs">Pop Songs</a> and number six on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100_Airplay" title="Billboard Hot 100 Airplay">Radio Songs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcharts_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcharts-26">[26]</a></sup> As of July 2009, "Womanizer" was listed at number thirty-nine in the best selling digital songs of all time, with sales over 2,777,600.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thirtynine_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-thirtynine-27">[27]</a></sup> As of March 2015, "Womanizer" has sold 3.5 million digital downloads in the United States, according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_sales_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-us_sales-1">[1]</a></sup> It is Spears' best-selling digital single in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_sales_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-us_sales-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Canada, the single topped the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a> on October 18, 2008, and stayed in the position for five consecutive weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcharts_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbcharts-26">[26]</a></sup> "Womanizer" entered the Australian charts on October 13, 2008 at number sixteen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Three weeks later, it peaked at number five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aus_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-aus-29">[29]</a></sup> It shipped over 70,000 copies, earning a <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" title="Music recording sales certification">platinum</a> certification by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> (ARIA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ariacertification_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-ariacertification-30">[30]</a></sup> In New Zealand, the song peaked at number nine on October 27, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nz_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-nz-31">[31]</a></sup> The song was certified gold according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_New_Zealand" title="Recording Industry Association of New Zealand">Recording Industry Association of New Zealand</a> (RIANZ), selling over 7,500 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rianzcerti_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-rianzcerti-32">[32]</a></sup> The track debuted at number four in the United Kingdom on November 9, 2008 and reached its peak position of number three four weeks later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uk_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-uk-34">[34]</a></sup> On January 16, 2009, it was certified silver by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI), with sales over 200,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpicertification_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpicertification-35">[35]</a></sup> According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Official_Charts_Company" title="The Official Charts Company">The Official Charts Company</a>, the song has sold 447,000 copies there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> "Womanizer" reached the peak in a number of European countries, including Belgium (Flanders), Denmark, Finland, France, Norway and Sweden. It also reached the top ten in Austria, Belgium (Wallonia), Czech Republic, Italy, Spain and the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ultratop_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-ultratop-37">[37]</a></sup> In addition, the track became Spears' sixth <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_number-one_hits_of_2008" title="List of European number-one hits of 2008">European number-one single</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcharts_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbcharts-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Working on 'Womanizer' with Joseph was a lot of fun. [...] He makes sure that he gets the types of shots that go with the music. It's not like a movie, it's more like a musical. You know, if I say 'on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hi-hat_(instrument)" title="Hi-hat (instrument)">hi-hat</a> here or on the drumbeat here, I want my leg to be in the air.' And it's that detail, and it does make a difference, and that's what he can do. It's very rare to find people that still know how to do that."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Spears about working with Joseph Kahn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>The music video was filmed on September 24 and 25, 2008 in Los Angeles, directed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kahn" title="Joseph Kahn">Joseph Kahn</a>, who previously worked with Spears for the music videos of "<a href="/wiki/Stronger_(Britney_Spears_song)#Music_video" title="Stronger (Britney Spears song)">Stronger</a>" and "Toxic".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pre_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-pre-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Kahn, Spears pitched him her original concept, which included all the main elements used in the final version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-40">[40]</a></sup> Spears thought of the video as a sequel to "Toxic", as seen in her documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Britney:_For_the_Record" title="Britney: For the Record">Britney: For the Record</a></i>, whereas Kahn approached it as "a 2008 answer" to the previous clip. He added that, "'Toxic' was a crystallization of her career at that time, [...] There are elements and moments of that I felt could [have been] improved. ['Womanizer'] is a bit more fashion-forward".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvd_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-dvd-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toxic_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-toxic-41">[41]</a></sup> About how the concept of the video related to their previous work, Kahn commented that "It's just a great girl fantasy. There are things she's really good at, like having a really natural knack for knowing what girls want. [...] It's a much more mature sound and much more mature lyrics, and she always has the greatest ideas. She's hyper-aware of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pop_culture" title="Pop culture">pop culture</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-toxic_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-toxic-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vma_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-vma-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>The costumes and looks for each of the different women were chosen by Spears and Kahn. The scenes in the <a href="/wiki/Sauna" title="Sauna">sauna</a> were suggested by Kahn, as a response to the attacks Spears received over the years about her weight. He stated, "I knew that the whole world would be watching, so I wanted something in there that stated, 'This is Britney, this is why you should respect her'". The set was cleared for two hours, leaving her and Kahn alone shooting the sequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vma_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-vma-42">[42]</a></sup> Kahn also decided to end the video with an image of Spears smiling, because "We just needed to tell everybody she's OK".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tsc_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-tsc-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>A censored version of the music video premiered on October 10, 2008 on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/20/20_(US_television_series)" title="20/20 (US television series)">20/20</a></i> at the end of their show. The uncensored version premiered on MTV the same night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-premiere_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Synopsis">Synopsis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Synopsis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Britney_as_womanizer.PNG"><img alt="Three upside down images of the upper bust of a woman. In the first image, she is blond and smiling, wearing a provocative slip nightgown. In the second image, her hair is a dark shade of red with a fringe and she is wearing a black corset with a white shirt underneath. She has necklaces on and her right arm is covered in tattoos. Her right arm is also holding a tray with a half-full glass. In the third image, she has a black bob haircut and her lips are red. She is wearing a striped shirt, a pencil skirt and horn rimmed glasses. She is singing and dancing provocatively to a blond man in front of her who wears a suit. Several people behind her are also wearing suits and dancing." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="162" data-file-width="300" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/71/Britney_as_womanizer.PNG/220px-Britney_as_womanizer.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/71/Britney_as_womanizer.PNG 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Britney_as_womanizer.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears in the sauna scene in the music video.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The video begins with an opening caption that reads "Womanizer". During the introduction, Spears is naked and smiling at a sauna, while covering herself with her hands. These scenes are seen throughout the video. When the first verse begins, the official version of Spears wearing a slip nightgown is making breakfast for her boyfriend (<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brandon_Stoughton" title="es:Brandon Stoughton">Brandon Stoughton</a>) as he gets ready for work. When he is at the office, he sees a new secretary, which is actually Spears in disguise wearing <a href="/wiki/Horn-rimmed_glasses" title="Horn-rimmed glasses">horn-rimmed glasses</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Pencil_skirt" title="Pencil skirt">pencil skirt</a>. She starts dancing in front of him and sings the chorus. She makes him follow her into the photocopier, where she photocopies her buttocks. On the back, we see an awkward-looking man, the same who appears in the plane scene on "<a href="/wiki/Toxic_(song)" title="Toxic (song)">Toxic</a>". Then, Spears is disguised as a red-haired, tattooed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waitress" title="Waitress">waitress</a> in a restaurant. She dances around him with her dancers and plays with him over the kitchen counter. After this, her boyfriend is seen getting driven home by Spears, disguised as a <a href="/wiki/Chauffeur" title="Chauffeur">chauffeur</a>. She starts to kiss him, driving the car with her heel until both get home. Once they get into the bedroom, Spears reveals that she was the three women he was "womanizing" all along. She then begins attacking her boyfriend. This is shown through Spears as her three alter egos, and then as the real version of herself. Spears throws a blanket over her boyfriend and makes the bed. The video ends with Spears smiling, and a repeat of the opening caption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-premiere_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-premiere-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Margeaux Watson of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> said the video "looks promising. [...] The dancing is stiff and minimal, a disappointment since her moves are her strong suit. But this is a welcome return to the Britney we love – gorgeous, gyrating, greased up, and gamely playing the vamp".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-ew-44">[44]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/OK!" title="OK!">OK!</a></i> commented that "in addition to seeing Brit in three different sexy getups, the video [...] features an oiled-up Britney writhing around in nothing but a smile".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ok_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-ok-45">[45]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> said the video was "a cross between 'Toxic' and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Office" title="The Office">The Office</a></i>" and added, "she’s dancing [and] looking like the old Britney".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Courtney Hazlett of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Msnbc.com" title="Msnbc.com">msnbc.com</a> claimed "When Spears isn’t shown naked and writhing in a steam room, she’s fired up".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbc_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc-47">[47]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/TV_Guide" title="TV Guide">TV Guide</a></i> writer Adam Bryant said that "the music video features some of the most strategically placed hands in music-video history [...] [The] video is quite a return to form for the troubled pop star".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tvguide_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-tvguide-48">[48]</a></sup> The music video for "Womanizer" became a worldwide success right after it premiered on the Internet, gaining seven million viewers in less than 48 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sevenmillion_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-sevenmillion-49">[49]</a></sup> The music video was listed as the best video of 2008 in polls by MTV and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fuse_TV" title="Fuse TV">Fuse TV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bestmtv_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-bestmtv-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fuse_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-fuse-51">[51]</a></sup> It won Music Video of the Year at the 2009 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NRJ_Music_Awards" title="NRJ Music Awards">NRJ Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrj_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrj-52">[52]</a></sup> The video was also nominated for <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Pop_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Pop Video">Best Pop Video</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year" title="MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year">Video of the Year</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2009_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2009 MTV Video Music Awards">2009 MTV Video Music Awards</a>. It lost the latter category to <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Single_Ladies_(Put_a_Ring_on_It)" title="Single Ladies (Put a Ring on It)">Single Ladies</a>", but won Best Pop Video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vma_2_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-vma_2-53">[53]</a></sup> Womanizer is already <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VEVO" title="VEVO">VEVOcertified</a> after reach 100 million views on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BritneyPOM17.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4896" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/BritneyPOM17.jpg/220px-BritneyPOM17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/BritneyPOM17.jpg/330px-BritneyPOM17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/BritneyPOM17.jpg/440px-BritneyPOM17.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BritneyPOM17.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spears during the performance of "Womanizer" on the <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a> residency concert.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The song was performed for the first time at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bambi_Awards" title="Bambi Awards">Bambi Awards</a> in Germany, on November 27, 2008. For the performance Spears wore hot pants, fishnet stockings and a black top hat. The ensemble was compared to the costume <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> wore during the first act of her <a href="/wiki/Sticky_%26_Sweet_Tour" title="Sticky &amp; Sweet Tour">Sticky &amp; Sweet Tour</a> (2008–09).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcbambi_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcbambi-55">[55]</a></sup> Spears was also presented with an award for Best International Popstar by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Lagerfeld" title="Karl Lagerfeld">Karl Lagerfeld</a>, who said, "I admire you ... not just for your art, but for your energy. [You are] coming back not only as a phoenix but as a bird of paradise".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-promotour_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-promotour-56">[56]</a></sup> The following night, Spears performed the song at <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Academy" title="Star Academy">Star Academy</a></i>, with similar choreography and dance moves but wearing a red strapless dress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-promotour_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-promotour-56">[56]</a></sup> On November 30, 2008, Spears performed at <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_TV_series)" title="The X Factor (UK TV series)">The X Factor</a></i>. The performance was watched by over thirteen million UK citizens, making it the most viewed episode in the show’s history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viewers_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-viewers-57">[57]</a></sup> On December 2, 2008, she performed the song at <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> along with a performance of "<a href="/wiki/Circus_(song)" title="Circus (song)">Circus</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mtvgma_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-mtvgma-58">[58]</a></sup> On December 15, 2008, she performed at the Japanese music show <i><a href="/wiki/Hey!_Hey!_Hey!_Music_Champ" title="Hey! Hey! Hey! Music Champ">Hey! Hey! Hey! Music Champ</a></i>. The following day, she performed at <i>NTV Best Artist 2008</i> in a black and gold bra, hot pants and a white top hat. She also sported a fake <a href="/wiki/Tattoo" title="Tattoo">tattooed</a> heart in her cheek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-japan_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-japan-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The song was a major part in <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a> (2009), as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encore_(concert)" title="Encore (concert)">encore</a> of the show. After a video interlude of Spears's music videos set to "<a href="/wiki/Break_the_Ice_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Break the Ice (Britney Spears song)">Break the Ice</a>" ended, Spears appeared wearing a police officer uniform designed by <a href="/wiki/Dean_and_Dan_Caten" title="Dean and Dan Caten">Dean and Dan Caten</a>, with black sunglasses, a hat with her trademark logo and sequined <a href="/wiki/Handcuffs" title="Handcuffs">handcuffs</a>. Her female dancers were also dressed as policewomen, while her male dancers were dressed as criminals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nme_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-nme-60">[60]</a></sup> During the performance, she danced and flirted with the male dancers. At the end of the song, she returned to the main stage while her dancers surrounded her and a shower of sparks fell over them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-sun-61">[61]</a></sup> She thanked the audience and bowed to each side of the arena. She left the stage with an instrumental version of "Circus" playing in the background.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usat_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-usat-62">[62]</a></sup> Jane Stevenson of the <i><a href="/wiki/Toronto_Sun" title="Toronto Sun">Toronto Sun</a></i> praised the performance for being a standout number in the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-sun-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Womanizer" was also performed at the <a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_Tour" title="Femme Fatale Tour">Femme Fatale Tour</a> (2011) as the last song of the fourth act. Following "<a href="/wiki/I_Wanna_Go" title="I Wanna Go">I Wanna Go</a>", which featured her dancing with members of the audience onstage, Spears performed "Womanizer" while surrounded by her dancers dressed as police officers. Shirley Halperin of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> stated that "[the] mid-tempo numbers [...] seemed to stall out quickly, where faster offerings like 'Womanizer,' 'I Wanna Go' and 'Toxic' had the sold out crowd jumping in place and pumping their number twos in the air."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Ed Masley of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Arizona_Republic" title="The Arizona Republic">The Arizona Republic</a></i> called the back-to-back performances of "I Wanna Go" and "Womanizer" "a triumphant double shot of dance-pop greatness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Keith Caufireld of <i>Billboard</i> said the performance "seemed a bit flat after the crowd-wowing 'I Wanna Go.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Spears is currently performing "Womanizer" as the second song for her Las Vegas residency, <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_AXIS" title="The AXIS">The AXIS</a> theater. She is accompanied by dancers clad in spandex outfits and masks, and walks on their backs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillboardReview_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-BillboardReview-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The song was later performed in a greatest hits medley, at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Billboard_Music_Awards" title="2016 Billboard Music Awards">2016 Billboard Music Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The song was also included in Spears's setlist for the <a href="/wiki/IHeartRadio_Music_Festival" title="IHeartRadio Music Festival">iHeartRadio Music Festival</a> on September 24th, 2016.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_versions">Cover versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cover versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"Womanizer" has been <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">covered</a> by many artists from a variety of <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">music genres</a>, as well as a great number of amateurs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cover_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-cover-68">[68]</a></sup> Clark Collis of <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> explained that "the song has been covered by other artists with an enthusiasm only matched in recent times by musicians’ desire to remake <a href="/wiki/Radiohead" title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>’s '<a href="/wiki/Creep_(Radiohead_song)" title="Creep (Radiohead song)">Creep</a>' in their own image".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ewcover_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-ewcover-69">[69]</a></sup> On December 8, 2008, New Zealand singer <a href="/wiki/Ladyhawke_(musician)" title="Ladyhawke (musician)">Ladyhawke</a> performed a cover at <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Live_Lounge" title="Live Lounge">Live Lounge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hawke_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-hawke-70">[70]</a></sup> The song was covered by American band <a href="/wiki/The_All-American_Rejects" title="The All-American Rejects">The All-American Rejects</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!_Music" title="Yahoo! Music">Yahoo! Music</a> <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi Smash</a> show in December 2008. It was performed in an acoustic version, in which the band members played percussions with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beer_bottles" title="Beer bottles">beer bottles</a>. The cover also included an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/The_Turtles" title="The Turtles">The Turtles</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Happy_Together_(song)" title="Happy Together (song)">Happy Together</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> British singer <a href="/wiki/Lily_Allen" title="Lily Allen">Lily Allen</a> also covered the song, because "simple really, I love Britney and I love the song".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cover_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-cover-68">[68]</a></sup> Her cover was a stripped down version, that according to Nick Levine of <a href="/wiki/Digital_Spy" title="Digital Spy">Digital Spy</a>, "might provoke those who reckon it doesn't have much of a chorus to revise their opinion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lily_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-lily-72">[72]</a></sup> Allen also performed the song as the encore during her <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lily_Allen_concert_tour_(2009)" title="Lily Allen concert tour (2009)">2009 tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lily2_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-lily2-73">[73]</a></sup> French singer <a href="/wiki/Sliimy" title="Sliimy">Sliimy</a> cover was deemed as an "<a href="/wiki/Indie_pop" title="Indie pop">indie</a> makeover".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cover_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-cover-68">[68]</a></sup> He would later be the opening act of the second Paris date at The Circus Starring Britney Spears.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sliimy_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-sliimy-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>On January 13, 2009, English singer <a href="/wiki/Ana_Silvera" title="Ana Silvera">Ana Silvera</a> covered the song during one of her London concerts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silvera_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-silvera-75">[75]</a></sup> On April 6, 2009, Scottish band <a href="/wiki/Franz_Ferdinand_(band)" title="Franz Ferdinand (band)">Franz Ferdinand</a> also covered the song at Radio 1's Live Lounge. Lead singer Alex Kapranos claimed "It's been the best song out in the last few months".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-franzone_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-franzone-76">[76]</a></sup> It was also covered regularly by them during their 2009 American spring tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-franztwo_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-franztwo-77">[77]</a></sup> The song was performed live by UK girl group <a href="/wiki/Girls_Aloud" title="Girls Aloud">Girls Aloud</a> during their <a href="/wiki/Out_of_Control_Tour" title="Out of Control Tour">Out of Control Tour</a>, starting April 24, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-girlsaloud_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-girlsaloud-78">[78]</a></sup> Their version was released on their 2009 live album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Out_of_Control:_Live_from_the_O2" title="Out of Control: Live from the O2">Out of Control: Live from the O2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-girlsaloudalbum_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-girlsaloudalbum-79">[79]</a></sup> "Womanizer" was also covered by <a href="/wiki/Fall_Out_Boy" title="Fall Out Boy">Fall Out Boy</a>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ewcover_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-ewcover-69">[69]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%22Weird_Al%22_Yankovic" title='"Weird Al" Yankovic'>"Weird Al" Yankovic</a> also covered this song for part of the polka medley off his 2011 album <i><a href="/wiki/Alpocalypse" title="Alpocalypse">Alpocalypse</a></i>. In the 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Britney_2.0" title="Britney 2.0">Britney 2.0</a>", actors <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Benoist" title="Melissa Benoist">Melissa Benoist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Newell" title="Alex Newell">Alex Newell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jenna_Ushkowitz" title="Jenna Ushkowitz">Jenna Ushkowitz</a> performed a cover of the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Track_listings">Track listings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Womanizer_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Track listings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">

<td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">

<li>
<dl>
<dt>CD single</dt>
</dl>
</li>
